## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (ODE rate laws)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is explicitly a time-derivative of concentration A, which is the standard setup for chemical kinetics modeled by ordinary differential equations. With only t and A available, the most likely relationships are classical rate laws where dA_dt depends on A (reaction order, autocatalysis, inhibition) and possibly explicitly on t (time-varying rate constants, external forcing).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order decay/production: dA_dt = c0 (constant-rate source/sink, e.g., photolysis at constant flux or zero-order consumption)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (unimolecular growth/decay; sign of c0 sets production vs decay)
- Second-order kinetics (self-reaction): dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular consumption/production involving A with itself)
- nth-order power-law: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general empirical reaction order)
- Linear with offset (source + first-order loss): dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A (constant inflow/outflow plus first-order reaction)
- Reversible first-order relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) (approach to equilibrium concentration c1 with rate constant c0)
- Autocatalytic (logistic-type in concentration space): dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating growth with finite limiting concentration)
- Cubic/quenching term: dA_dt = c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (growth with nonlinear self-inhibition or bimolecular loss competing with production)
- Rational inhibition (self-inhibited rate): dA_dt = c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate saturates with A due to limiting step or self-inhibition-like form)
- Rational with squared inhibition (stronger suppression): dA_dt = c0 * A / (A**2 + c1) (high-A suppression stronger than linear denominator)
- Time-dependent rate coefficient (aging/deactivation/forcing): dA_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * A (effective first-order rate drifting over time)
- Periodic forcing / modulated kinetics: dA_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A (e.g., light/dose cycling causing time-varying pseudo-first-order rate)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt is approximately constant over A, a zero-order term c0 indicates a constant source/sink independent of concentration.
- If dA_dt is proportional to A (straight line through origin in dA_dt vs A), c0 * A indicates first-order kinetics; the sign of c0 distinguishes decay vs growth.
- If dA_dt scales like A**2 at larger A, c0 * A**2 suggests bimolecular/self-reaction or recombination losses.
- A stable fixed point at A = c1 with dA_dt changing sign around it suggests relaxation form c0 * (c1 - A).
- A peak rate at intermediate A (dA_dt rises then falls vs A) is consistent with autocatalytic/limiting form c0 * A * (c1 - A) or c0 * A - c1 * A**2.
- If dA_dt increases with A but levels off at high A, a saturating rational form c0 * A / (A + c1) is indicated (rate-limiting step / effective saturation).
- If high A strongly suppresses the rate (faster-than-linear inhibition), denominators like (A**2 + c1) can capture stronger quenching/termination behavior.
- If the relationship between dA_dt and A changes systematically over time (different apparent slopes at different t), an explicit time-varying coefficient such as (c0 + c1 * t) * A or (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A is a plausible structure.

f(t,A)= -0.1286242133\,\sqrt{A}\;-\;0.1286242133\,A\,e^{-0.0593843782\,t}\;+\;0.3894244877\,\sin(0.5829315814\,A).

So any matching candidate must be able to represent **simultaneously**:
1) a \(\sqrt{A}\) term with a **negative** coefficient,  
2) an \(A\exp(k t)\) term with \(k=-0.05938...\) and negative coefficient,  
3) a pure \(\sin(\omega A)\) term with **no phase shift** and amplitude \(0.3894...\),  
and **no extra terms** (no constants, logs, rational terms, extra exponentials in \(A\), etc.), unless they can be set to zero by parameters.

### Candidate 1: `sqrt(A)*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*sin(A*c4 + c5)`

- Has \(A e^{c2 t}\): set \(c2=-0.0593843782\), \(c1=-0.1286242133\).

- No extra terms. **Matches.**

### Candidate 2: `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + A**c2*c3 + c4*sin(A*c5 + c6) + c7*log(A*c8 + 1)`

- Actually this candidate can match too (no extra unavoidable terms). **Matches.**
